Litigation Management and Defense Administration
THIS FORM IS PART OF THE POLICY AND MUST BE READ WITH THE DECLARATIONS AND ENDORSEMENTS.

Our organization assumes the exclusive authority to manage the legal response to any qualified liability demand presented against your enterprise.

This authority encompasses the complete direction of all litigation strategies, settlement negotiations, and the selection of appropriate legal representation.

When a qualified legal action is initiated, we will appoint legal counsel to represent your interests in the pending judicial proceedings.

The selection of the defense attorney remains entirely within our discretion, utilizing our network of approved legal professionals and specialized firms.

You may request the appointment of specific counsel; however, we are under no obligation to honor such requests unless mandated by jurisdiction.

The appointed legal counsel will focus solely on defending the allegations that fall within the scope of this commercial liability contract.

We maintain the authority to investigate any claim or suit at our discretion, utilizing internal personnel or independent investigative resources.

During the course of the litigation, we will determine the most appropriate legal strategy to mitigate potential financial exposures.

We possess the unilateral authority to negotiate and finalize the settlement of any claim or suit without requiring your explicit consent.

Our settlement decisions are based on a comprehensive evaluation of liability exposure, anticipated litigation costs, and jurisdictional venue factors.

If we determine that a negotiated resolution is the most prudent course of action, we will execute the settlement on your behalf.

Our obligation to provide legal representation ceases immediately upon the exhaustion of the applicable limit scheduled in the policy declarations.

Once the relevant limit has been entirely depleted through the payment of judgments or settlements, we will withdraw from the defense.

You will be formally notified in writing when the applicable limit is approaching exhaustion and when it has been fully depleted.

Following the depletion of the limit, the responsibility for funding any ongoing legal representation transfers entirely to your organization.

In situations where a lawsuit contains both covered allegations and allegations excluded by this contract, we will provide a defense for the entire action.

However, we reserve the right to issue a formal reservation of rights regarding the specific allegations that fall outside the coverage scope.

This reservation of rights ensures that our provision of a defense does not constitute a waiver of our right to deny financial responsibility.

We will not provide financial reimbursement for any judgments or settlements associated with the uncovered portions of the legal action.

You retain the option to hire independent legal counsel, at your own expense, to monitor the litigation and advise you on uncovered exposures.

Any independent counsel retained by your organization must fully cooperate with the primary defense attorney appointed by our claims department.

The primary defense attorney retains ultimate control over the direction of the litigation and the presentation of the defense in court.

We will not reimburse any legal fees, consultation costs, or administrative expenses incurred by your independently retained legal counsel.

If a conflict of interest arises that legally requires the appointment of independent defense counsel, we will fund such representation at prevailing rates.

The prevailing rates for independent counsel will be determined based on standard legal fees for similar litigation within the specific geographic venue.

We require the independent counsel to adhere to our standard litigation management guidelines and billing protocols throughout the duration of the case.

Any failure by the independent counsel to comply with these administrative guidelines may result in the reduction or denial of fee reimbursements.

The administration of the defense process is designed to protect both your organizational assets and our financial interests under this contract.

We will keep your designated organizational representative reasonably informed regarding significant developments and major strategic decisions during the litigation process.

Ultimately, the final determination regarding trial progression versus settlement resolution rests exclusively with our claims administration personnel.

Investigation Assistance and Insured Cooperation Conditions
THIS FORM IS PART OF THE POLICY AND MUST BE READ WITH THE DECLARATIONS AND ENDORSEMENTS.

1. Your active and transparent participation in the fact-finding process is a mandatory requirement for the continuation of any liability protection.

The administrative framework of this contract relies upon your full cooperation to accurately assess the circumstances surrounding any reported incident.

When requested by our claims personnel, you must promptly provide access to all relevant organizational records, documents, and electronic data.

This includes, but is not limited to, employee training logs, maintenance schedules, operational manuals, and internal incident investigation reports.

2. You must facilitate interviews between our investigators and any of your employees, contractors, or agents who may possess relevant knowledge.

These interviews may be conducted in person, via telephone, or through virtual platforms, depending on the logistical requirements of the investigation.

If we deem it necessary, you and your employees must submit to formal examinations under oath regarding the details of the incident.

These examinations under oath will be recorded, and you may be required to sign a transcript verifying the accuracy of your statements.

3. You must assist our representatives in securing physical evidence and identifying third-party witnesses who can corroborate your version of events.

When requested, you must grant our investigators and retained experts unrestricted access to the physical premises where the incident occurred.

This access is necessary to conduct site inspections, take precise measurements, and perform forensic evaluations of the incident location.

During the course of any formal legal proceedings, your ongoing cooperation remains a critical condition of the provided defense services.

4. You must attend all required legal hearings, depositions, mediation sessions, and trial proceedings as directed by the appointed defense counsel.

Your organization must ensure that key personnel are available to testify truthfully and accurately regarding the facts of the case.

We will reimburse your organization for reasonable travel expenses and lost earnings incurred directly as a result of attending these required proceedings.

The maximum daily reimbursement rate for lost earnings is strictly capped at the amount specified in the administrative schedules.

5. You are expressly prohibited from taking any actions that might prejudice our ability to defend the claim or negotiate a favorable settlement.

Any intentional misrepresentation of facts, concealment of evidence, or collusion with the claimant will result in the immediate forfeiture of protection.

You must not enter into any agreements with third parties that attempt to assign liability or alter the legal dynamics of the claim.

If you possess any contractual rights to seek indemnification or financial recovery from another entity, you must preserve those rights entirely.

6. You are required to assist us in enforcing any such recovery rights against third parties who may be responsible for the incident.

This includes providing necessary documentation and testimony to support subrogation actions initiated by our legal recovery department.

Any financial recovery obtained from third parties will be distributed according to the specific recovery provisions outlined elsewhere in this contract.

Your failure to maintain comprehensive operational records may hinder the defense process and complicate the resolution of the liability demand.

7. We expect your organization to maintain standard commercial documentation practices consistent with your specific industry classification and operational scope.

If your lack of cooperation materially prejudices our ability to investigate or defend the action, we may formally deny the claim.

A determination of material prejudice is based on whether your actions or inactions significantly impaired the legal defense or increased the financial exposure.

We will issue formal written warnings if we determine that your level of cooperation is insufficient or detrimental to the ongoing investigation.

8. Continued non-compliance after the issuance of a formal warning will trigger a comprehensive review of your eligibility for ongoing liability protection.

The obligations detailed in this section apply equally to the primary named enterprise and any additional entities scheduled for protection.

Defense Expense Allocation and Claim Administration
THIS FORM IS PART OF THE POLICY AND MUST BE READ WITH THE DECLARATIONS AND ENDORSEMENTS.

A. This section details the financial frameworks concerning the administration of legal expenses and the allocation of associated administrative costs.

The costs associated with investigating and defending a qualified liability demand are classified as allocated loss adjustment expenses.

These allocated expenses typically include attorney fees, court filing costs, expert witness retainers, and specialized forensic investigation charges.

Unless explicitly modified by a separate schedule, the payment of these allocated loss adjustment expenses does not reduce the available liability limit.

We will fund the necessary premiums for appeal bonds or bonds required to release property attachments associated with the defended litigation.

B. However, our obligation to fund these bond premiums is strictly limited to the portion of the bond that corresponds to the available limit.

We are under no obligation to furnish the actual bond or provide collateral to secure the issuance of any required financial guarantees.

Any administrative expenses incurred by our internal claims personnel during the routine handling of the file are not charged to your organization.

If a judicial verdict is rendered against your enterprise, we will manage the calculation and payment of applicable post-judgment interest.

Our responsibility for post-judgment interest applies only to the portion of the judgment that falls within the available scheduled limit.

C. This interest obligation ceases immediately once we have paid, offered to pay, or deposited our respective portion of the judgment with the court.

In scenarios involving multiple protected entities, the allocation of defense expenses requires careful administrative coordination and oversight.

If both your organization and an additional scheduled entity are named in the same lawsuit, we will typically appoint a single defense firm.

The appointment of unified counsel is designed to streamline the defense strategy and minimize redundant legal expenditures during the proceedings.

If a legally recognized conflict of interest prevents unified representation, we will allocate separate counsel for each protected entity.

D. The costs associated with separate legal representation will be managed in accordance with the standard expense protocols established by our organization.

When a liability demand triggers protection under multiple distinct insurance contracts, a formal coordination of benefits process must be initiated.

You are required to promptly disclose the existence of any other active insurance policies that may apply to the reported incident.

We will analyze the respective provisions of all applicable contracts to determine the appropriate priority of financial responsibility.

If this contract is determined to provide primary protection, we will administer the defense and fund the associated expenses accordingly.

E. If this contract is determined to provide excess protection, our financial obligations will not commence until the primary limits are fully exhausted.

During the period of excess application, we retain the right to monitor the primary litigation but will not fund the active defense expenses.

We may voluntarily contribute to the defense costs in an excess capacity if we determine that such participation protects our financial interests.

Any voluntary contribution to defense expenses does not alter the fundamental priority of coverage or create an ongoing obligation to fund the litigation.

In situations where multiple primary policies exist, we will seek to allocate the defense expenses proportionally among the participating carriers.

F. This proportional allocation is typically based on the ratio of each carrier's available limit to the total available limits of all primary policies.

We reserve the right to initiate arbitration or legal proceedings against other carriers to enforce appropriate expense allocation and recovery.

Your organization must fully cooperate with our efforts to coordinate benefits and recover allocated expenses from other responsible insurance entities.

The administrative procedures outlined herein ensure the equitable distribution of legal costs while maintaining the integrity of the provided liability protection.

All expense payments and administrative allocations are subject to continuous internal audit to verify compliance with our litigation management standards.

Notice of Premium Audit and Accounting Procedures
POLICYHOLDER NOTICE - INFORMATION ABOUT YOUR POLICY

This notice outlines the mandatory accounting and premium audit procedures applicable to your commercial general liability coverage part.

The premium amounts displayed on the declarations pages are advance estimates derived entirely from the exposure information you provided at inception.

The actual final premium obligation will be calculated after the policy period ends through a comprehensive and detailed audit of your business records.

You are contractually obligated to maintain detailed, accurate, and organized records of all business operations, employee payroll, gross sales, and subcontracted costs.

These essential business records must be securely preserved for a minimum of three years following the expiration or cancellation date of this policy.

We explicitly reserve the right to examine and audit your financial and operational records at any reasonable time during the active policy period.

Furthermore, we may conduct subsequent audits up to three years after the final termination date of the applicable coverage part.

The official audit process may involve a physical inspection of your scheduled premises, a thorough review of tax documents, or an examination of accounting ledgers.

If the final computed premium determined by the audit exceeds the initial advance premium, you will be billed directly for the additional amount due.

Payment for any additional premium generated by the final audit calculation is due immediately upon your receipt of the final billing statement.

Conversely, if the final computed premium is less than the advance premium, we will refund the unearned premium portion directly to the first named insured.

All premium refunds remain strictly subject to any minimum retained premium conditions or absolute minimums specified elsewhere in the coverage documents.

Failure to comply promptly with our audit requests constitutes a material breach of the fundamental policy conditions and obligations.

In the event of your non-compliance, we may apply a non-cooperation penalty surcharge or estimate the final premium based on maximum projected operational exposures.

An estimated final premium generated due to non-cooperation may significantly exceed your actual operational exposure and resulting financial obligation.

You must notify our underwriting department promptly if your core business operations change materially at any point during the active policy period.

Material changes requiring notification include the addition of new business classifications, expansion into new rating territories, or significant unexpected increases in total payroll.

Accurate classification of your daily operations is absolutely essential for correct premium calculation and the proper applicability of liability coverage.

We maintain the authority to reclassify your operations during the final audit if the actual business activities differ from the classifications initially shown in the schedules.

Subcontractor records must clearly and unequivocally demonstrate whether the hired subcontractors carried their own adequate and active liability insurance during the project.

If a subcontractor fails to provide valid proof of concurrent insurance, their total cost of work will be included in your primary premium calculation.

Valid certificates of insurance from all independent contractors and subcontractors must be collected and verified prior to the commencement of their respective work.

These collected certificates must be retained in your permanent files and presented immediately to our designated auditor upon formal request.

Any disputed audit findings must be submitted to our accounting department in writing within thirty days of receiving the final premium billing statement.

Your written dispute must include specific, verifiable documentation supporting your alternative premium calculation and challenging the auditor's findings.

All undisputed portions of the final audit billing remain fully due and payable while the disputed items are under active internal review.

We will review the submitted documentation carefully and issue a final, binding determination regarding the disputed premium amounts within sixty days.

If an independent outside vendor is utilized to conduct the premium audit, they act entirely as our authorized representative for the purpose of data collection.

You must provide the exact same level of cooperation and access to our authorized external vendors as you would directly to our internal audit personnel.

The specific exposure bases listed in the rating schedules are the sole metrics used to determine the final cost of this commercial insurance transaction.

Please review your initial policy schedules carefully upon receipt to ensure all exposure estimates align accurately with your projected business activities for the year.

Contact your authorized insurance broker or designated agent immediately if you discover any discrepancies or errors in the advance premium calculation or classification assignments.

This endorsement addresses PFAS Exclusion under form CG 00 01 edition 01 24.

2. This endorsement modifies the commercial general liability coverage part and applies to all operations, classifications, and locations scheduled on the policy.

The provisions contained herein establish an absolute exclusion for liabilities connected to perfluoroalkyl and polyfluoroalkyl substances, regardless of the exposure basis.

Coverage does not apply to any bodily injury or property damage arising out of the actual, alleged, or threatened presence of these chemicals.

The exclusion equally applies to personal and advertising injury claims stemming from the distribution, sale, or handling of products containing such materials.

3. For the purposes of this endorsement, the excluded substances are defined as any chemical compound containing at least one fully fluorinated carbon atom.

This definition encompasses, but is not limited to, perfluorooctanoic acid, perfluorooctanesulfonic acid, and any of their respective salts, isomers, or degradation products.

The carrier bears no obligation to provide indemnification for any loss, cost, or expense related to the specified chemical compounds.

Furthermore, the carrier assumes no responsibility to defend any suit, action, or proceeding seeking damages attributable to the excluded substances.

4. The restriction extends to any discharge, dispersal, seepage, migration, release, or escape of the chemicals into the environment, including indoor air quality.

Coverage is excluded whether the introduction of the substances was sudden, accidental, gradual, or occurred over an extended period of time.

No coverage is provided for any request, demand, order, or statutory requirement that any insured or others test for or monitor the substances.

Similarly, costs associated with cleaning up, removing, containing, treating, detoxifying, or neutralizing the specified chemicals are entirely excluded from this policy.

5. Claims made by or on behalf of any governmental authority for damages resulting from testing, monitoring, or remediation are also excluded.

Any product, material, or good manufactured, sold, handled, distributed, or disposed of by the insured containing these chemicals falls under this restriction.

Liability assumed under any contract or agreement regarding the remediation or containment of these chemicals is similarly excluded from coverage.

This endorsement supersedes any other provision, endorsement, or exception that might otherwise grant coverage for environmental or pollution-related exposures.

6. The restriction applies to operations conducted at scheduled premises, temporary worksites, and all products and completed operations hazards.

If any portion of a claim involves allegations both related and unrelated to the excluded substances, the carrier will not allocate defense costs.

Instead, the entire claim shall be deemed excluded if the primary or underlying allegation stems from the presence of the specified chemicals.

Insureds are expected to maintain accurate records of materials used in their manufacturing, distribution, or contracting processes to verify compliance.

7. Failure on the part of the insured to identify the presence of these chemicals in raw materials does not invalidate this exclusion.

The carrier reserves the right to deny indemnification for any settlement reached without prior written consent regarding these specific chemical liabilities.

This exclusion applies to all exposure bases, including gross sales, payroll, area, and cost of work, regardless of premium calculation methods.

Any exception to pollution exclusions found elsewhere in the policy documentation does not apply to the chemical compounds defined herein.

8. The provisions set forth in this endorsement are absolute and apply to all operations, classifications, and territories associated with the insured business.

In the event that any court or jurisdiction finds a portion of this exclusion unenforceable, the remaining provisions shall remain in full effect.

Damages encompass statutory fines, penalties, punitive assessments, and multiplied damages levied by governmental bodies or regulatory agencies concerning the excluded substances.

The exclusion applies regardless of whether the substances were introduced into the environment by the named insured or by any third party.

9. No coverage exceptions apply for the completed operations hazard or the products hazard when the underlying injury involves the specified chemical compounds.

This endorsement controls over any conflicting provisions in the coverage part and applies consistently across all scheduled limits and classifications.

A. Classification And Exposure Reference

This form applies to Property owners - commercial buildings at Location 5, territory 012, using class code 97047.

The rating schedule shows area of 130,133, a damage to premises rented to you limit of $100,000, and premium $1,457.

This endorsement addresses Designated Professional Services Exclusion under form CG 21 67 edition 04 13.

This endorsement modifies the commercial general liability coverage part and applies to the specific operations or classifications designated in the accompanying schedules.

B. The provisions herein restrict the scope of coverage available for certain specialized activities.

No coverage is afforded for bodily injury or property damage originating from the performance or omission of any professional service.

This restriction applies equally to personal and advertising injury originating from the same performance or omission of professional duties.

The term professional service encompasses any activity requiring specialized knowledge, advanced training, or licensed expertise in a specific field of practice.

Examples of such restricted activities include the preparation or approval of maps, shop drawings, opinions, reports, or surveys.

C. Supervisory, inspection, architectural, or engineering activities are strictly excluded from the liability framework provided by this coverage part.

Medical, surgical, dental, x-ray, or nursing services fall entirely outside the scope of protection.

Any instructional, educational, or consulting services provided by the named insured or on the named insured's behalf are similarly restricted.

The exclusion operates regardless of whether the professional service is a primary component of the business operations or an incidental activity.

Claims alleging negligent hiring, employment, training, or supervision of individuals performing these restricted services will not trigger the defense or indemnity provisions.

D. If a claim involves both ordinary negligence and professional negligence, the entire claim shall be excluded if the ordinary negligence is intertwined with the professional service.

The carrier assumes no obligation to investigate, settle, or defend any suit or demand that involves allegations rooted in the designated professional services.

Costs and attorney fees incurred in responding to such allegations must be borne solely by the named insured.

This restriction applies to any individual or organization qualifying as an insured under the liability framework, including employees, volunteer workers, and executive officers.

When the designated professional services are performed by independent contractors or subcontractors on behalf of the named insured, the exclusion remains fully applicable.

E. The classification code and exposure basis shown in the rating schedule do not override or negate the application of this professional services restriction.

Even if a premium charge is developed based on gross sales or payroll associated with the professional activity, the liability exclusion remains absolute.

No exception is granted for bodily injury occurring on the described premises if the proximate cause is the rendering of the specialized service.

The products-completed operations hazard does not encompass any injury or damage resulting from the failure of the professional service to meet expected standards.

Any warranties or representations made regarding the quality, fitness, or performance of the professional service are excluded from the scope of the liability framework.

F. Data privacy violations, unauthorized access to confidential information, and similar cyber events arising during the professional service are not addressed by this endorsement.

The carrier reserves the right to withdraw from the defense of any litigation upon determining the facts fall within this restriction.

Notice of such withdrawal will be provided to the named insured in accordance with the administrative conditions governing communication and correspondence.

The named insured is responsible for maintaining separate professional liability or errors and omissions coverage to address the exposures excluded by this endorsement.

The existence or absence of such separate professional liability coverage has no bearing on the interpretation or enforcement of this specific exclusion.

G. In the event of a dispute regarding the classification of an activity as a professional service, the customary standards of the relevant industry will be considered.

However, the final determination of whether an activity constitutes a professional service under this policy rests upon the definitions and restrictions outlined herein.

The application of this endorsement supersedes any conflicting language found in the primary liability coverage forms or previously issued amendatory documents.

The remaining provisions, limits, and conditions of the commercial general liability coverage part continue in full force and effect without alteration.

Classification Assignment and Exposure Valuation Rules
THIS FORM IS PART OF THE POLICY AND MUST BE READ WITH THE DECLARATIONS AND ENDORSEMENTS.

1. Classification codes are assigned to the commercial enterprise based on the primary nature of the business operations conducted at the scheduled premises.

The classification schedule serves as the foundation for determining the appropriate rating factors and exposure bases utilized in the premium calculation process.

A single commercial location may be subject to multiple classification codes if the enterprise conducts distinctly separate and independent business operations.

The assignment of multiple classifications requires the enterprise to maintain strictly segregated payroll and revenue records for each distinct operational category.

2. If the enterprise fails to maintain segregated records, the carrier will assign the highest rated classification code to the entirety of the exposure.

Standard exception classifications, such as clerical office employees and outside sales personnel, may be assigned separately if their duties are strictly limited.

Clerical office employees must perform their duties in an area physically separated from the primary manufacturing or mercantile operations of the business.

The carrier retains the exclusive authority to determine the final classification codes applicable to the commercial enterprise based on factual operational data.

3. If an inspection reveals a material deviation from the anticipated operations, the carrier will issue a retroactive endorsement correcting the classification schedule.

Material changes in business operations must be reported to the carrier immediately to ensure the proper classification codes are applied to the risk.

Territory assignments are determined by the physical address of the scheduled premises or the geographic region where the principal operations are executed.

Operations conducted outside the designated territory shown in the schedules may be subject to different rating multipliers or specific coverage restrictions.

4. When the exposure basis is designated as gross sales, the valuation includes all amounts charged for merchandise sold and services performed.

Inter-departmental transfers and internal accounting transactions do not constitute gross sales and are excluded from the final exposure valuation.

When the exposure basis is designated as payroll, the valuation encompasses the total remuneration distributed to all active employees and corporate officers.

Executive officer remuneration is subject to specific minimum and maximum valuation caps as determined by the prevailing state rating bureau guidelines.

5. When the exposure basis is designated as area, the valuation is calculated using the total square footage of the buildings occupied by the enterprise.

The area calculation includes all basements, storage facilities, and outbuildings utilized in connection with the primary commercial operations of the business.

When the exposure basis is designated as the cost of work, the valuation includes the total cost of all labor, materials, and equipment.

The cost of work valuation specifically encompasses all payments made to subcontractors, regardless of whether they provide their own materials or equipment.

6. The enterprise may not deduct the cost of materials supplied directly to subcontractors from the final cost of work exposure valuation.

Certain specialized classifications may utilize alternative exposure bases such as the number of admissions, total units produced, or specific event duration.

The precise definition of any alternative exposure basis will be detailed in a separate amendatory endorsement attached to the primary policy documents.

Classification descriptions are generalized summaries of typical business operations and do not explicitly define the parameters of the provided insurance protection.

7. The presence of a specific classification code on the schedule does not override any explicit exclusion or limitation contained within the policy text.

The carrier may reclassify the enterprise mid-term if a newly enacted regulatory statute alters the standard classification system utilized by the industry.

Any mid-term reclassification mandated by regulatory changes will be applied on a pro-rata basis from the effective date of the new statute.

The enterprise may request a formal review of their assigned classifications by submitting a detailed narrative description of their daily business activities.

8. The carrier will evaluate all classification review requests and issue a written determination affirming or modifying the current schedule within thirty days.

Approved classification modifications requested by the enterprise will be applied prospectively unless the carrier determines a retroactive adjustment is warranted.

Administrative Conditions and Contractual Obligations
THIS FORM IS PART OF THE POLICY AND MUST BE READ WITH THE DECLARATIONS AND ENDORSEMENTS.

A. This document constitutes the entire agreement between the commercial enterprise and the carrier regarding the provision of commercial liability insurance.

No modifications, amendments, or waivers of any policy provision will be considered valid unless formally issued by the carrier as a written endorsement.

The first named insured designated on the declarations page acts as the sole authorized representative for all entities protected under this agreement.

The carrier will direct all administrative correspondence, billing statements, and formal notices exclusively to the mailing address of the first named insured.

By accepting this policy, the first named insured affirms that all statements and representations made during the application process are entirely accurate.

B. The carrier has issued this policy in direct reliance upon the factual accuracy of the representations provided by the commercial enterprise.

Intentional misrepresentation or the concealment of material facts concerning the business operations may result in the immediate voiding of this insurance contract.

The first named insured may cancel this policy at any time by returning the original documents or providing advanced written notice of termination.

The carrier may cancel this policy by mailing a formal notice of termination to the first named insured at the last known address.

Cancellation for the non-payment of premium requires a minimum notice period of ten days prior to the effective date of the termination.

C. Cancellation for any reason other than non-payment requires a minimum notice period of thirty days prior to the effective date of termination.

If the policy is cancelled by the enterprise, the carrier will calculate the return premium utilizing the standard short-rate penalty computation method.

If the policy is cancelled by the carrier, the return premium will be calculated on a strictly proportional pro-rata basis without penalty.

The carrier retains the right to inspect the scheduled premises and ongoing operations of the enterprise at any reasonable time during the term.

These inspections are conducted solely for the purpose of determining insurability, evaluating operational hazards, and calculating appropriate premium charges.

D. The carrier does not warrant that the premises are safe, healthful, or in compliance with any local, state, or federal safety regulations.

The enterprise must promptly notify the carrier of any fundamental changes in ownership, management structure, or primary business operations.

The rights and duties established under this policy cannot be transferred to another entity without the express written consent of the carrier.

In the event of the death of the first named insured, the rights and duties will automatically transfer to the appointed legal representative.

The legal representative will possess the authority to act on behalf of the enterprise only while performing duties strictly related to the estate.

E. Until a legal representative is formally appointed, temporary authority will be granted to any individual maintaining temporary custody of the commercial property.

The enterprise must take all reasonable precautions to prevent further incidents or subsequent damages following any initial event that may trigger this policy.

The carrier will not be responsible for any subsequent damages resulting from the failure of the enterprise to implement reasonable preventative measures.

Any legal action initiated against the carrier must be commenced within two years following the date the disputed incident or damage occurred.

The enterprise must fully comply with all terms, conditions, and administrative requirements of this policy before initiating any legal action against the carrier.

F. In the event of multiple entities being designated as named insureds, the financial obligations regarding premium payment remain joint and several.

The carrier may elect not to renew this agreement by mailing a formal notice of non-renewal to the first named insured.

Notices of non-renewal will be dispatched at least thirty days prior to the scheduled expiration date of the current policy term.

Proof of mailing the cancellation or non-renewal notice to the designated address will serve as sufficient proof of notification under this contract.

Any specific state statutes that conflict with these administrative conditions will automatically supersede the printed text to ensure strict regulatory compliance.

Application of Scheduled Limits and Aggregate Depletion
THIS FORM IS PART OF THE POLICY AND MUST BE READ WITH THE DECLARATIONS AND ENDORSEMENTS.

The numerical values displayed on the limits schedule represent the absolute maximum financial responsibility assumed by the carrier under this specific contract.

These scheduled maximums apply regardless of the number of protected entities, the number of individuals injured, or the number of claims filed.

The general aggregate limit establishes the maximum amount the carrier will disburse for all combined incidents occurring during the active policy period.

This general aggregate maximum encompasses all financial responsibilities except those specifically allocated to the products and completed operations hazard category.

As disbursements are made to resolve qualifying incidents, the remaining available balance of the general aggregate limit is correspondingly depleted.

Once the general aggregate limit is entirely exhausted by cumulative disbursements, the carrier holds no further obligation to respond to subsequent incidents.

The products and completed operations aggregate limit functions independently and establishes a separate maximum for incidents arising from distributed goods or finished work.

Disbursements allocated to the products and completed operations category do not reduce the available balance of the general aggregate limit.

The each occurrence limit defines the maximum financial responsibility for all damages arising out of a single, continuous, or repeated exposure event.

The each occurrence limit remains subject to the available remaining balance of the applicable aggregate limit at the time the incident is resolved.

If multiple scheduled locations are designated on the declarations, the general aggregate limit may be modified to apply separately to each distinct premises.

The separate application of the aggregate limit per location must be explicitly authorized by a designated endorsement attached to the policy documents.

The personal and advertising injury limit establishes the maximum disbursement available for all offenses committed against any single person or organization.

This specific limit is also subordinate to the general aggregate limit and will be restricted by any prior depletion of that overall maximum.

The medical expense limit provides a designated sub-limit for immediate medical costs incurred by third parties, regardless of established fault.

Disbursements made under the medical expense sub-limit are automatically deducted from the available balance of the each occurrence limit.

The damage to premises rented to you limit establishes a specific maximum for fire-related incidents occurring at leased commercial facilities.

This leased premises sub-limit applies strictly to the specific location where the enterprise maintains a formal lease agreement and conducts daily operations.

The scheduled limits apply exclusively to incidents that occur entirely within the designated coverage territory defined in the primary policy text.

Incidents occurring outside the designated territory will not be evaluated against the scheduled limits unless a specific international endorsement is attached.

The concept of severability of interests ensures that the scheduled limits apply separately to each protected entity facing a formal claim.

However, the application of severability does not increase the absolute maximum limits of insurance available for any single occurrence or aggregate period.

If a single incident triggers multiple sub-limits, the carrier will not disburse an amount exceeding the highest applicable single limit of insurance.

The enterprise cannot combine or stack the limits of multiple consecutive policy periods to resolve a single, continuous exposure event.

Continuous exposure events spanning multiple policy periods will be assigned exclusively to the single policy period where the damage first became evident.

The carrier will provide written notification to the first named insured when any aggregate limit has been depleted by more than fifty percent.

A final written notification will be issued immediately upon the complete exhaustion of any aggregate limit scheduled on the declarations page.

Any supplementary payments or administrative expenses incurred by the carrier during the resolution process do not reduce the scheduled limits of insurance.

The limits of insurance will automatically reset to their full scheduled value at the inception of each new annual renewal period.

Modifications to the scheduled limits requested mid-term will apply only to incidents occurring after the effective date of the approved change endorsement.

Premium Audit and Accounting Provisions
PREMIUM, AUDIT, AND ACCOUNTING CONDITIONS
Named insured
Juniper Gate Learning Center, LLC
Policy term
04/01/2026 - 04/01/2027
Scheduled premium
See declarations and premium schedules
Audit basis
Records described in the audit conditions

1. The premium shown on the declarations page represents an advance deposit calculated entirely from your initial estimated exposure bases at inception.

Final premium calculations occur only after the policy period concludes and rely heavily on a comprehensive actual audit of your operational records.

You must maintain detailed accounting ledgers that properly segregate all exposures by classification, territory, and specific location for our eventual review.

We reserve the absolute right to examine and reproduce your financial records at any reasonable time during the active policy term.

2. This vital examination right extends for a period of up to three full years following the expiration or cancellation of this insurance contract.

Acceptable records for this purpose include federal tax returns, detailed payroll registers, daily sales journals, subcontractor invoices, and valid certificates of insurance.

If you fail to provide adequate documentation during our review, we may apply the highest rated classification to all unverified operational exposures.

Advance premiums are systematically credited against the final computed premium determined by our internal audit department at the close of the term.

3. Should the final computed premium exceed the initial advance deposit, you must remit the outstanding balance in full within thirty calendar days.

Conversely, if the audited premium is less than the initial deposit, we will return the unearned portion directly to the first named insured.

We may elect to waive a physical field audit and instead accept a voluntary statement of exposures submitted by your accounting department.

Voluntary exposure statements must be signed by an authorized corporate officer and remain strictly subject to future verification by our field auditors.

4. In the event of policy cancellation prior to the expiration date, the final premium will be calculated on a standard pro-rata basis.

However, if the first named insured initiates the mid-term cancellation, a customary short-rate penalty may apply to the final premium calculation.

Subcontractor costs must be clearly documented, including absolute proof that such entities carried their own adequate liability insurance during the active project.

Without valid certificates of insurance on file, subcontractor costs will be treated as direct employee payroll and rated accordingly under this policy.

5. You are strictly required to notify our accounting department immediately if your projected operational exposures increase by more than twenty percent.

Interim premium adjustments may be billed during the policy term to accurately reflect substantial increases in operational scale or newly added classifications.

Failure to pay final audit balances constitutes a material breach of contract and may result in immediate cancellation of any active renewal policies.

Disputed audit findings must be submitted in writing within fifteen days of receiving the final premium adjustment statement from our billing department.

6. The formal dispute notice must identify the specific classifications or exposure amounts in question and include all relevant supporting financial documentation.

While a formal dispute is pending review, you remain responsible for under applicable law the undisputed portion of the final premium balance immediately.

Our audit department will issue a formal written resolution within forty-five days of receiving a complete and properly documented dispute package.

If the accounting dispute is resolved entirely in your favor, any overpaid premium amounts will be credited or refunded promptly to your account.

7. Any unpaid audit balances forwarded to an external collection agency will accrue additional administrative fees and statutory interest charges where permitted.

The minimum retained premium specified in the declarations will apply regardless of the final audited exposure amounts or mid-term cancellation requests.

Joint ventures and newly acquired organizations must be reported separately to ensure accurate premium allocation across multiple distinct corporate entities.

Remuneration calculations must include all monetary compensation, performance bonuses, housing allowances, and substitute labor costs as defined by applicable state regulations.

8. We assume no responsibility for identifying classification errors that result in overpayment if you fail to provide accurate initial operational descriptions.

This comprehensive audit provision supersedes any conflicting payment terms or conditions found elsewhere in the commercial general liability coverage parts.

Assignment and Transfer of Policy Administration
THIS FORM IS PART OF THE POLICY AND MUST BE READ WITH THE DECLARATIONS AND ENDORSEMENTS.

A. Rights and duties established under this commercial general liability contract cannot be transferred to another party without our written consent.

Any attempted assignment or transfer of policy benefits lacking our express written authorization shall be considered void and legally unenforceable.

The named insured cannot sell, assign, or otherwise transfer their interest in this insurance policy as part of a corporate transaction.

In the event of a merger or acquisition, the surviving entity does not automatically inherit the protections of this specific policy.

A formal request for transfer must be submitted to our underwriting department along with complete details of the proposed ownership change.

B. We reserve the absolute right to approve or deny any transfer request based on our evaluation of the new risk profile.

An exception to this strict prohibition exists in the event of the death of an individual designated as the first named insured.

If an individual named insured dies, their rights and duties are temporarily transferred to their legal representative or estate executor.

This temporary transfer of rights applies only while the legal representative is acting within the scope of their official duties.

Until a legal representative is formally appointed, anyone having proper temporary custody of the deceased insured's property assumes the policy duties.

C. The temporary custodian is bound by all policy conditions, including the obligation to report incidents and cooperate with our investigations.

Coverage for the legal representative or temporary custodian extends only to operations previously conducted by the deceased individual named insured.

No new business ventures or expanded operations initiated by the estate will be protected under the existing commercial liability framework.

Bankruptcy or insolvency of the insured does not relieve us of our obligations under this commercial general liability contract.

However, a bankruptcy trustee does not gain the authority to expand the scope of operations beyond those scheduled in the declarations.

D. The appointment of a receiver or liquidator requires immediate notification to our administrative offices to ensure proper policy documentation.

Premium payment obligations remain fully enforceable against the estate, the bankruptcy trustee, or the legal representative managing the insured entity.

Any pending premium audits will be directed to the legal representative, who must provide access to all necessary financial records.

The transfer of policy administration duties does not alter the applicable limits, exclusion parameters, or classification codes established at inception.

If a corporate named insured undergoes a name change without a change in ownership structure, an amendatory endorsement is required.

E. Name changes must be reported within thirty days to ensure continuous alignment between the policy documents and the legal entity.

The addition of new subsidiaries or newly formed organizations is governed by separate provisions and does not constitute a transfer.

We will not recognize any third-party claims of policy ownership based on private contractual agreements between the insured and outside entities.

Indemnification agreements signed by the named insured do not transfer the actual policy rights to the indemnified third party.

Additional insured status must be achieved through specific endorsement scheduling rather than an attempted blanket assignment of the primary policy.

F. Any approved transfer of rights will be memorialized through a formal endorsement issued by our home office and attached to the policy.

The effective date of an approved transfer will be explicitly stated on the issued endorsement, superseding any prior private arrangements.

Following a transfer, the new first named insured assumes full responsibility for all past and future premium obligations and audit adjustments.

The new entity also inherits the responsibility to distribute cancellation notices or policy changes to any other scheduled insured parties.

We maintain the right to conduct a comprehensive risk control survey of the new entity before finalizing any transfer of rights.

G. Failure to disclose material changes in operations during a transfer request constitutes grounds for immediate rescission of the transfer endorsement.

Territorial Application and State Provisions
THIS FORM IS PART OF THE POLICY AND MUST BE READ WITH THE DECLARATIONS AND ENDORSEMENTS.

The provisions of this policy apply exclusively to incidents, operations, or offenses that take place within the authorized geographic boundaries.

These boundaries generally encompass the United States of America, its incorporated territories and possessions, Puerto Rico, and the nation of Canada.

Operations conducted outside of these primary geographic areas are strictly excluded unless specifically addressed by a separate international endorsement.

International airspace and international waters are included only if the injury or damage occurs during direct travel between authorized jurisdictions.

Products manufactured or sold within the primary geographic boundaries may retain coverage if they are subsequently transported to foreign locations.

However, this product-related extension applies only if the original manufacturing or initial sale occurred within the authorized domestic territories.

Short-term international business travel by the named insured or their employees is accommodated under specific, limited circumstances outlined herein.

The activities of employees traveling abroad must be strictly limited to administrative, clerical, or executive duties on behalf of the insured.

Manual labor, construction activities, or physical service operations performed outside the authorized geographic boundaries will not receive liability protection.

Digital operations and internet activities present unique geographic challenges that require specific jurisdictional parameters for liability protection to apply.

Offenses related to electronic publications or digital advertising are considered to occur globally, provided the insured's business is based domestically.

Despite any global digital exposure, we require that any resulting litigation be formally filed and pursued within the authorized primary territories.

We will not participate in, fund, or recognize lawsuits brought in foreign courts or under the jurisdiction of foreign legal systems.

Any judgments, settlements, or legal costs awarded by tribunals outside the United States, its territories, Puerto Rico, or Canada are excluded.

If a lawsuit is filed domestically but involves international elements, we will evaluate the claim based strictly on domestic legal standards.

State-specific amendatory provisions may alter the application of these territorial rules depending on the primary mailing address of the named insured.

When state laws mandate broader geographic recognition for certain classes of business, those statutory requirements will supersede our standard limitations.

Currency fluctuations and international exchange rates will not alter the maximum financial limits scheduled in the commercial general liability declarations.

All premium calculations, audit adjustments, and claim settlements will be processed exclusively in the official currency of the United States.

If a domestic judgment involves foreign currency calculations, the exchange rate published on the date of the final judgment will apply.

Coverage is categorically suspended in any region, country, or territory subject to comprehensive trade sanctions or embargoes by the federal government.

We will not process payments or provide legal resources if doing so would violate established economic sanctions or international trade restrictions.

The insured must ensure that their export activities comply with all federal regulations regarding restricted nations and prohibited foreign entities.

Any liability arising from deliberate violations of international trade laws or customs regulations falls entirely outside the scope of this policy.

Vendors or distributors operating exclusively in foreign markets cannot be added as additional insureds under this domestic liability framework.

Cross-border transportation of hazardous materials requires specialized documentation and may be subject to strict territorial exclusions at the border crossing.

Incidents occurring at border checkpoints or customs facilities will be evaluated based on the exact physical location of the occurrence.

The burden of proof rests on the insured to demonstrate that an incident occurred within the authorized geographic boundaries.

Location schedules attached to the declarations dictate the primary premises, but the territorial rules govern off-site operations and mobile equipment.

Ambiguities regarding the exact location of an incident will be resolved by referencing official geographic coordinates and established international borders.

Maintaining accurate records of international shipments and employee travel is essential for determining the applicability of these territorial provisions.

Interpretation of Policy Provisions and Conflicting Forms
THIS FORM IS PART OF THE POLICY AND MUST BE READ WITH THE DECLARATIONS AND ENDORSEMENTS.

1. This commercial general liability contract is a composite document consisting of declarations, schedules, broad coverage parts, conditions, and specialized endorsements.

When evaluating the scope of protection, the policy must be read as a complete, integrated instrument rather than isolated independent clauses.

Provisions found in one section of the policy may be heavily modified, restricted, or entirely replaced by text in another section.

The declarations pages serve as the primary index, identifying the specific forms, limits, and classifications that apply to the scheduled operations.

2. Classification and territory entries are used primarily for rating purposes and do not independently determine or expand the scope of coverage.

The applicable coverage part, scheduled limit, specific exclusion, and attached endorsement must always be read in conjunction with the declarations.

In the event of a direct contradiction between the main coverage form and an attached endorsement, the endorsement will generally control.

Endorsements are designed to tailor the generic policy language to the specific risk profile and operational needs of the named insured.

3. A form listed for an exposure item may apply exclusively to the scheduled operation, specific location, or completed-operations hazard shown.

Broad exclusionary endorsements take precedence over any implied protections found within the standard definitions or insuring agreements of the base forms.

If multiple exclusionary endorsements apply to a single incident, the most restrictive language will dictate the final determination of the claim.

Schedule entries containing specific location addresses limit the application of certain forms to operations conducted strictly at those designated premises.

4. When a specific provision conflicts with a general provision within the same document, the specific provision will be given interpretive priority.

State amendatory endorsements are attached to ensure the policy complies with the unique statutory and regulatory requirements of the governing jurisdiction.

If any standard policy language conflicts with a mandatory state amendatory endorsement, the state-specific provisions will automatically override the standard text.

We continuously monitor legislative changes, but if a policy clause violates current law, it will be enforced as if appropriately amended.

5. The severability of interests clause ensures that the policy applies separately to each insured against whom a formal claim is brought.

However, this severability principle does not increase the maximum aggregate limits or per-occurrence limits scheduled in the commercial liability declarations.

Section headings, titles, and formatting choices are provided solely for navigational convenience and do not alter the actual contractual obligations.

The use of bold text or quotation marks indicates that a word or phrase is specifically defined within the policy definitions section.

Undefined terms will be interpreted according to their standard, everyday dictionary meanings within the context of commercial insurance industry practices.

6. Any typographical errors or formatting inconsistencies discovered in the policy documents will not invalidate the clear intent of the underwriting agreement.

The named insured is responsible for reviewing all schedules, forms, and endorsements immediately upon receipt to ensure accuracy and completeness.

Discrepancies between the requested coverage and the issued policy documents must be reported to our administrative offices within thirty days.

We rely entirely on the accuracy of the information provided during the application process when assembling these specific policy forms.

7. Material misrepresentations regarding the nature of the business may render certain coverage forms inapplicable or void the policy in its entirety.

When an endorsement removes a specific exclusion, it does not automatically grant coverage if another unamended exclusion applies to the situation.

The reinstatement of a previously excluded peril requires explicit affirmative language within the endorsement, not merely the deletion of negative text.

Our claims department relies on the exact edition dates of the forms attached to the policy when evaluating incident reports.

8. Prior editions or outdated industry standard forms hold no interpretive weight if they differ from the specific versions scheduled herein.

Final authority regarding the interpretation of conflicting forms rests with the established legal precedents of the jurisdiction governing this insurance contract.

Vermont Amendatory Provision - Cancellation and Nonrenewal Procedures
THIS ENDORSEMENT CHANGES THE POLICY. PLEASE READ IT CAREFULLY.

A. This amendatory document modifies the cancellation, nonrenewal, and conditional renewal provisions applicable to your commercial general liability coverage part.

All conflicting provisions regarding the termination or modification of coverage found elsewhere in the policy packet are replaced by the following stipulations.

The first named entity shown in the declarations may cancel this policy by mailing or delivering advance written notice of termination.

The written notice submitted by the first named entity must specify the future date when the termination of coverage becomes effective.

We may cancel this policy by mailing or delivering a formal written notice of termination directly to the first named entity.

B. If our cancellation is due to the nonpayment of premium, we will provide notice at least fifteen days before the effective date.

When our cancellation is for any reason other than nonpayment of premium, we will provide notice at least forty-five days in advance.

Notice of cancellation will be mailed to the last known mailing address of the first named entity and the producer of record.

We will obtain a certificate of mailing or maintain verifiable electronic records proving the dispatch of the termination notice.

The formal notice will state the effective date of cancellation, and the active policy period will end on that specified date.

C. If this policy is cancelled prior to expiration, we will calculate the return premium and send it to the first named entity.

If we initiate the cancellation, the return premium will be calculated on a proportional basis for the unexpired policy term.

If the first named entity initiates the cancellation, the return premium may be calculated utilizing a customary short rate penalty factor.

The cancellation will remain effective even if we have not yet made or offered a refund of the unearned premium balance.

We may elect not to renew this policy by mailing or delivering a written notice of nonrenewal to your address.

D. Notice of nonrenewal will be provided to you at least forty-five days before the expiration date of the current policy period.

If the nonrenewal notice is mailed less than forty-five days before expiration, the coverage will remain in effect for forty-five days.

The earned premium for any extended period of coverage will be calculated using the rates applicable to the expiring policy term.

We are not obligated to send a notice of nonrenewal if you have accepted replacement coverage from another carrier.

We are also not obligated to send a nonrenewal notice if you have agreed in writing not to renew the coverage.

E. Any notice of nonrenewal issued by us will include the underwriting reason for our decision not to extend the coverage period.

The stated reasons for nonrenewal must be based on objective underwriting criteria or adverse changes in the scheduled commercial exposures.

If a local jurisdiction statute requires a longer notice period or restricts the reasons for cancellation, those statutory requirements will control.

Verifiable proof of mailing will serve as sufficient proof of notice for both cancellation and nonrenewal communications under this commercial contract.

Any unearned premium refund due to you will be processed and dispatched within thirty days after the effective date of termination.

F. The designated producer of record does not possess the authority to reinstate coverage once a formal cancellation notice has been issued.

Reinstatement of a previously cancelled policy requires our explicit written consent and may necessitate the payment of all outstanding premium balances.

If a specific location or classification is deleted from the schedules by endorsement, it does not constitute a cancellation of the policy.

Partial deletions of coverage parts or locations will be processed as routine policy endorsements rather than full policy cancellations.

This amendatory provision applies exclusively to the commercial general liability coverage part and does not alter the rules for other lines.

Aggregate Limits and Allocation Provisions
THIS FORM IS PART OF THE POLICY AND MUST BE READ WITH THE DECLARATIONS AND ENDORSEMENTS.

The limits of insurance specified in the declarations dictate the maximum financial responsibility assumed under this commercial general liability contract.

These scheduled amounts apply regardless of the number of insured persons, claims made, or individuals seeking financial recovery.

The General Aggregate limit represents the absolute ceiling for all damages payable during a single annual term, excluding specific designated hazards.

Payments made to resolve claims or satisfy judgments steadily erode the General Aggregate balance available for subsequent incidents.

Once the General Aggregate limit is completely exhausted by the payment of damages, all associated protection ceases immediately.

The Products-Completed Operations Aggregate limit operates independently from the General Aggregate and applies strictly to the corresponding hazard.

Damages arising from goods manufactured, sold, or distributed, as well as work that has been finished, erode this separate aggregate.

The classification of a claim into either the general operations category or the completed operations category determines which aggregate is depleted.

The Each Occurrence limit establishes the maximum payable amount for any single event or series of continuous and repeated exposures.

This occurrence cap applies independently to every distinct incident, provided the relevant aggregate limit has not yet been exhausted.

If a single occurrence triggers damages that exceed this per-event cap, the remainder of the financial burden falls outside the contract scope.

The Personal and Advertising Injury limit restricts the payable damages for offenses such as libel, slander, or copyright infringement.

This specific limit applies per person or organization offended, rather than per occurrence, subject always to the overarching General Aggregate.

Medical payments limits, if scheduled, are typically sub-limits that are included within, and not in addition to, the Each Occurrence maximum.

Damage to premises rented to the named insured is governed by a separate sub-limit applicable only to specific fire or water events.

The depletion of any limit is driven solely by the payment of damages and does not typically include the costs associated with legal defense.

Legal defense expenses are generally handled outside the limits of insurance unless a specific endorsement alters this standard arrangement.

In situations where defense costs are brought within the limits, every dollar spent on legal fees directly reduces the available aggregate.

The limits of insurance apply separately to each consecutive annual period and to any remaining period of less than twelve months.

If the term is extended by an endorsement for a fraction of a year, the limits do not automatically reinstate or increase.

The allocation of damages across multiple annual periods may be necessary when continuous injury spans several consecutive terms.

Under no circumstances will the limits of multiple consecutive contracts be stacked to artificially inflate the available financial protection.

When an injury is determined to have occurred over multiple terms, the maximum recovery is restricted to the highest single applicable limit.

The scheduling of limits relies on the accurate disclosure of all material operational risks at the inception of the contract.

Requests to increase the limits of insurance mid-term are subject to comprehensive underwriting review and require written approval.

Any approved increase in limits will only apply to occurrences that take place after the effective date of the modifying endorsement.

Deductibles or self-insured retentions, if applicable, must be satisfied by the named insured before any limit of insurance is accessed.

The application of a deductible does not increase the total limit of insurance available for the remainder of the claim.

We maintain the authority to settle any claim within the applicable limits without requiring the explicit consent of the named insured.

The exhaustion of the applicable aggregate limit immediately terminates our obligation to investigate, defend, or resolve any pending or future claims.

Separation of Insureds and Additional Insured operation
THIS FORM IS PART OF THE POLICY AND MUST BE READ WITH THE DECLARATIONS AND ENDORSEMENTS.

1. The commercial general liability contract clearly distinguishes between the primary named insured and other parties who may receive incidental protection.

The named insured is the entity explicitly listed on the declarations page and bears the primary administrative responsibilities for the contract.

These administrative duties include the payment of all premiums, the reporting of operational changes, and the maintenance of accurate exposure records.

Additional insureds are external individuals or organizations granted specific, limited protection through the attachment of a designated endorsement.

2. The protection afforded to an additional insured is strictly confined to the parameters outlined in the specific modifying form.

Commonly, additional insured status is granted to project owners, lessees, or general contractors who require protection arising from the named insured operations.

The scope of this external protection is generally limited to vicarious liability stemming directly from the acts or omissions of the named insured.

Independent acts of negligence committed solely by the additional insured are routinely excluded from the scope of the provided protection.

3. The separation of insureds provision ensures that the contract applies separately to each individual or entity claiming protection.

This severability principle means that a breach of a condition by one insured does not automatically void the protection for another innocent insured.

Furthermore, the separation of insureds allows one protected party to bring a valid claim against another protected party under the same contract.

Despite this cross-liability application, the separation provision does not multiply or increase the maximum limits of insurance available.

4. The Each Occurrence and applicable Aggregate limits remain fixed, regardless of how many insured entities are implicated in a single event.

Additional insured endorsements often distinguish between ongoing operations and the products-completed operations hazard.

Protection for ongoing operations ceases the moment the specific project is finished or the named insured departs the job site.

To secure protection for liabilities arising after project completion, a specific completed operations additional insured endorsement must be attached.

5. Primary and non-contributory conditions are frequently requested by external parties seeking additional insured status on the contract.

When this condition is properly endorsed, the protection provided by this contract will respond before any other insurance available to the additional insured.

We will not seek contribution from the additional insured own liability policies if the primary and non-contributory requirement is met.

The granting of primary status is contingent upon the existence of a written contract requiring such an arrangement prior to the loss.

6. Every insured, whether named or additional, has independent duties in the event of an incident, claim, or legal proceeding.

Immediate written notice of any event that may result in a claim must be provided to the administrative processing center.

The failure of the named insured to provide notice does not excuse an additional insured from fulfilling their own reporting obligations.

All protected parties must cooperate fully in the investigation, settlement, or defense of the claim as requested by the claim administrators.

7. No insured may voluntarily make any payment, assume any obligation, or incur any expense without our prior written authorization.

Any unauthorized financial commitments made by an insured will be their sole responsibility and will not be reimbursed.

The cancellation of the contract by the named insured immediately terminates the protection for all additional insureds simultaneously.

We are not obligated to provide separate notices of cancellation to additional insureds unless explicitly mandated by a specific endorsement.

8. The rights and duties of the named insured cannot be transferred to another party without our explicit written consent.

In the event of the named insured death or bankruptcy, temporary administrative rights may transfer to a legal representative.

Exclusions and Endorsement Precedence
THIS FORM IS PART OF THE POLICY AND MUST BE READ WITH THE DECLARATIONS AND ENDORSEMENTS.

A. The commercial general liability contract is constructed through a combination of base coverage forms, schedules, and modifying endorsements.

Endorsements are specialized forms that alter, restrict, or expand the provisions found within the standard base coverage documents.

When a conflict arises between the language in a base form and the language in an attached endorsement, the endorsement takes precedence.

Exclusionary endorsements are specifically designed to remove protection for certain hazards, activities, or exposures that fall outside the underwriting appetite.

The attachment of a specific exclusion supersedes any broad grant of protection that might otherwise appear to apply to the situation.

B. Exclusions are applied to eliminate overlapping protection that should be properly addressed by a different type of insurance contract.

For example, liabilities arising from the use of automobiles are excluded here because they belong on a commercial auto policy.

Similarly, obligations to injured employees are excluded from general liability because they are the domain of workers compensation frameworks.

Certain environmental hazards, such as the gradual release of pollutants or toxic chemicals, are subject to absolute exclusionary language.

Occupational disease exposures involving specific harmful substances like silica, asbestos, or heavy metals are routinely removed from the scope of protection.

C. Liabilities stemming from the unauthorized access to, or disclosure of, confidential personal information are excluded to avoid overlapping with cyber liability products.

Employment-related practices, including wrongful termination, discrimination, and workplace harassment, are explicitly excluded from the general liability framework.

The application of an exclusion is evaluated based on the proximate cause of the injury or damage, regardless of how the legal complaint is drafted.

If an excluded hazard is determined to be the primary driver of the loss, the entire claim may fall outside the scope of the contract.

Some exclusions contain specific exceptions that restore a limited degree of protection under very narrow, strictly defined circumstances.

D. The burden of proving that a claim falls within the broad grant of protection rests entirely upon the party seeking the financial benefit.

Conversely, the burden of proving that a specific exclusion applies to remove that protection rests with the administrative claim examiners.

Materiality plays a significant role in the evaluation of exclusions and the overall scope of the liability contract.

A material change in the risk profile, such as the introduction of a new excluded hazard, can severely impact the availability of protection.

Endorsements must be properly scheduled on the declarations or a supplementary forms list to be considered a valid part of the contract.

E. The edition date of each form and endorsement is critical for determining the exact contractual language in effect at the time of the loss.

Insurance forms are periodically updated by regulatory and advisory organizations to address emerging legal precedents and shifting risk landscapes.

The specific edition date listed in the schedule controls the interpretation of the provision, even if a newer version exists in the marketplace.

Upon renewal of the annual term, outdated forms may be replaced with newer editions, potentially altering the scope of the exclusions.

The named insured is responsible for reviewing the schedule of forms and endorsements at each renewal to understand any reduction in protection.

F. Notices of material reduction are provided during the renewal process to highlight significant changes to the exclusionary language.

Severability clauses within certain exclusions may preserve protection for one insured party even if the exclusion applies strictly to another.

However, absolute exclusions generally apply to all insured parties uniformly, regardless of their individual involvement in the excluded activity.

Any modification to an exclusionary endorsement requires mutual agreement and the issuance of a revised schedule by the underwriting department.

Verbal agreements or representations made by brokers cannot override the written exclusionary language contained within the scheduled endorsements.
